         </div>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202403841-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/f00b3572-ada0-4fbd-b5b6-7b57d93b9edc/adfm202403841-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/f00b3572-ada0-4fbd-b5b6-7b57d93b9edc/adfm202403841-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/580d361f-30ec-41bc-bb65-a9ab447ae887/adfm202403841-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/f00b3572-ada0-4fbd-b5b6-7b57d93b9edc/adfm202403841-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202403841-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202403841" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The initial charge/discharge curves of the pristine HC and Pre-HC half-cells. b) Comparison of the initial specific capacity and ICE obtained from pristine HC and Pre-HC half-cells. c) The OCV and the pre-sodiation efficiency of HC and Pre-HC half-cells. CV curves of the pristine HC and Pre-HC half-cells for d) the 1<sup>st</sup> and e) the 2<sup>nd</sup> cycle. f) Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients of the pristine HC and the pre-sodiated HC anodes from GITT measurements.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The cyclic voltammograms of pristine HC and Pre-HC half-cells are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0004">4d,e</a>. During the first CV curve, the pristine HC shows three reduction peaks (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0004">4d</a>), and the broad peak at ≈1.0&nbsp;V corresponds to the reduction of electrolyte and irreversible reactions of the HC matrix,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0040_R_d212906234e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - Carbon Energy">40</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0041_R_d212906234e1124" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - ACS Energy Lett.">41</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> while this reduction peak disappears in both Pre-HC anodes due to the pre-formed SEI and C─O─Na component evidenced by TEM and XPS results (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0003">3</a>), and the intensities of oxidation peak at 0.3&nbsp;V in the 1<sup>st</sup> cycle and redox peaks in the 2<sup>nd</sup> cycle maintain equally for pristine and Pre-HC anodes, which means the pre-sodiation process has no negative effects on the electrochemical performance of HC for the following cycle. The rate performances of the pristine HC and Pre-HC anodes are shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> (Supporting Information). All anodes exhibit equal specific charge capacities at 0.05&nbsp;C, while two Pre-HC anodes present a little larger specific charge capacity at a higher rate due to the pre-formed artificial SEI layer, which is similar to the results reported by Zhen Wang<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0031_R_d212906234e1140" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Energy Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Hengyi Fang.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0032_R_d212906234e1146" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Angew. Chemie – Int. Ed.">32</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Galvanostatic Intermittent Titration Technique (GITT) curves in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0004">4f</a> indicate that the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient of Pre-HC anodes maintains well without changes if compared to the pristine HC in the range of 10<sup>−13</sup>–10<sup>−11</sup>&nbsp;cm<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, indicating that the structure of HC maintains well after SSE pre-sodiation with Na metal thin film.</p>
         
         <p>The effects of this SSE pre-sodiation on the electrochemical performance of full cells were investigated as shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5</a>, and Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) is used as the cathode material with the anode/cathode capacity ratio of 1.15 (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting information). Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5a</a> shows the initial charge/discharge curves of full cells with the pristine HC and Pre-HC anodes at 0.05&nbsp;C, the specific charge/discharge capacity of the full cell with the pristine HC is 108.4/66.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, with the ICE of 61.0% due to the large irreversible capacity of HC, the initial specific discharge capacities of full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes increase to 88.5 and 102.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. Meanwhile, the ICEs are improved from 61.0% to 82.4% and 94.0% for full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes, respectively. The energy densities of full cells are improved from 126.5 to 161.3 and 214.4&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> for full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes (based on the total mass of anode and cathode active materials). Besides, the cycling stability is also improved after 50 cycles at 0.2&nbsp;C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5b</a>), the full cell with the pristine HC shows a specific discharge capacity of 30.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with a capacity retention rate of 54.5% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5c</a>), while full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes show specific discharge capacities of 44.3 and 69.8&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> with the capacity retention rates of 60.3% and 69.1%, respectively. Therefore, SSE pre-sodiation not only improves the initial specific discharge capacity and ICE of full cells but also provides a favorable capacity retention capability.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202403841-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/bfec567e-85dc-4d1a-8a7d-4a20030fc401/adfm202403841-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/bfec567e-85dc-4d1a-8a7d-4a20030fc401/adfm202403841-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/da669e72-5897-4b75-a8bc-733c299e43f1/adfm202403841-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/bfec567e-85dc-4d1a-8a7d-4a20030fc401/adfm202403841-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202403841-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202403841" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The initial charge/discharge curves of full cells. b) Cycling performance of full cells at 0.05&nbsp;C for the initial 2 cycles and 0.2&nbsp;C for the following cycles. c) The capacity retention performance of full cells at 0.2&nbsp;C. The Nyquist plots of full cells at the d) 3<sup>rd</sup> and e) 50<sup>th</sup> cycle and the corresponding fitting results of f) R<sub>SEI</sub> and g) R<sub>ct</sub>. h) The initial charge/discharge curves of full cells with the pristine HC anode and Pre-HC anodes after being stored in dry air (relative humidity: 1%) for 2 and 4&nbsp;h, i) the corresponding specific capacity of Na calculated by the specific capacity difference.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was performed to better understand the preferable electrochemical performance. The Nyquist plots of full cells with the pristine HC and Pre-HC anodes after the 3<sup>rd</sup> and the 50<sup>th</sup> cycles at a fully charged state are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5d,e</a>, respectively. The corresponding equivalent circuit is shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a> (Supporting information), the small semicircle at the high-frequency region and the broad semicircle at the middle frequency arise from Li<sup>+</sup> migration resistance across SEI and charge transfer resistance between electrode/electrolyte interface, respectively. The oblique line at low frequency is associated with Warburg impedance from solid diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup> in active materials.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0042" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0042_R_d212906234e1252" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 42 - Small">42</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The fitting R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>ct</sub> results are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5f,g</a>, respectively. After the 3<sup>rd</sup> cycle, full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na (120.5&nbsp;Ω) and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na (96.5&nbsp;Ω) anodes exhibit lower R<sub>ct</sub> than that of the full cell with pristine HC (199.6&nbsp;Ω) due to the improved reversible capacity and state of charge (SOC). In contrast, the R<sub>SEI</sub> values of full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na (4.9&nbsp;Ω) and HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na (8.4&nbsp;Ω) anodes are larger than that of the full cell with the pristine HC (3.8&nbsp;Ω), which means the SEI in Pre-HC possesses distinctive characteristics from that of electrochemically formed one in the pristine HC. After the 50<sup>th</sup> cycle, full cells with the pristine HC show both sharp growth of R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>ct</sub>. The R<sub>SEI</sub> of the full cell with pristine HC anode increased by 1.8&nbsp;Ω (from 3.8 to 5.6&nbsp;Ω), and the R<sub>ct</sub> increased by 272&nbsp;Ω (from 199.6 to 471.6&nbsp;Ω), indicating a continuous growth of SEI and capacity loss due to the instability of the electrochemical formed SEI. This phenomenon is consistent with the low capacity retention rate of the full cell in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5c</a>. In comparison, the variation trend of R<sub>SEI</sub> and R<sub>ct</sub> is distinct for full cells with Pre-HC anodes. Full cells with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and with HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes show 73.3 and 17.2&nbsp;Ω&nbsp;R<sub>ct</sub> growth, respectively, indicating that the growth of R<sub>ct</sub> is inhibited. The R<sub>SEI</sub> of HC-1&nbsp;µm Na increased by 0.9 Ω (from 4.9 to 5.8&nbsp;Ω). However, the R<sub>SEI</sub> of HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na decreased by 4 Ω (from 8.4 to 4.3&nbsp;Ω). This anomalous R<sub>SEI</sub> variation trend for the full cell with Pre-HC anode should be related to the its unique SEI composition and structure, as we would discuss in the following parts. These results demonstrate that i) The pre-formed SEI is unique and beneficial to the electrochemical performance; ii) SSE pre-sodiation can improve the cycling performance of full cells with both reduced impedance of Na<sup>+</sup> passing through SEI and charge transfer processes.</p>
         
         <p>The air stability of the pre-sodiated anode is also one critical factor for practical application. Although different kinds of anode pre-sodiation strategies have been proposed in previous works, the air stability of pre-sodiated anode is always ignored. The battery assembly process is usually carried out at a dew-point temperature below ─45&nbsp;°C (relative humidity: 0.31%). Here, the air stability of the HC anode after pre-sodiation was investigated, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5h,i</a>. Based on the irreversible capacity changes of the half cells (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0004">4</a>), we can determine that the pre-sodiation capacity of Pre-HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anode is 1115.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>Na</sub><sup>−1</sup>, which accounts for 95.7% of the theoretical capacity of Na metal (1165.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>Na</sub><sup>−1</sup>). The Pre-HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anode was stored in a dry air atmosphere (dew-point temperature: −35&nbsp;°C, relative humidity: 1%) for 2 and 4&nbsp;h to examine its air stability. And the retained pre-sodiation capacity of Pre-HC is calculated based on the initial specific discharge capacities of full cells (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5h</a>). After storing the Pre-HC in dry air for 2&nbsp;h, the specific capacity of Na reduces to 671.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>Na</sub><sup>−1</sup>, which may be attributed to the chemical reactions of the Pre-HC with O<sub>2</sub>, CO<sub>2</sub>, and H<sub>2</sub>O in air. When the storing time increases to 4&nbsp;h, the Pre-HC shows a specific capacity of 418.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>Na</sub><sup>−1</sup>, which is still larger than most cathode pre-sodiation additives (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting information). Therefore, this SSE pre-sodiation strategy, which shows high pre-sodiation efficiency and acceptable air stability, has great potential for industrial application.</p>
         
         <p>To elucidate the effect of pre-sodiation on the SOC of the cathode and anode during charge and discharge processes, the full cell in Swagelok-type was assembled with HC anode, NVP cathode, and Na metal reference electrode. This three-electrode cell was cycled between 3.75 and 1.75&nbsp;V at 0.05&nbsp;C, and the cell structure is shown in <b>Figures</b> <a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6a</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a> (Supporting information). During charge and discharge, both the relative voltage between NVP vs. HC and HC vs. Na are monitored, and the voltages of the cathode and anode are obtained separately. Since the NVP cathode only possesses one plateau capacity at ≈3.4&nbsp;V with less voltage change, the HC anode with more variable voltage evolution is considered the research focus in the full cell cycling. The voltage profile of the full cell with the pristine HC is shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6b</a>. The initial voltage of the pristine HC is 2.912&nbsp;V, and the discharging/charging cut-off voltages are 0.070&nbsp;V/1.614&nbsp;V. For the full cell with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na anode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6c</a>), the OCV of anode reduces to 0.895&nbsp;V, and the discharging and charging cut-off voltages fall to 0.047 and 1.569&nbsp;V, respectively. After pre-sodiation with 2.3&nbsp;µm Na, lower OCV (0.564&nbsp;V) and discharging/charging cut-off voltages (0.034&nbsp;V/1.358&nbsp;V) is observed with the increased pre-sodiation degree (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6d</a>). The lower charging cut-off voltage of Pre-HC suggests extra sodium can be stored in the HC matrix for the initial cycle and act as the reserve to make up for the capacity loss during cycling. This should be beneficial for improving the capacity retention rate of the full cell with pre-sodiation. According to the adsorption-intercalation-nanopore filling mechanism,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0043" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0043_R_d212906234e1359" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 43 - Chem. Mater.">43</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the capacity of HC can be divided into slope and plateau regions, i) the slope capacity (≥0.1&nbsp;V vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), which is derived from the adsorption of Na<sup>+</sup> at the surface of open pores and defect sites of graphene sheets and the insertion of Na<sup>+</sup> between graphene layers; ii) the plateau capacity (&lt;0.1&nbsp;V vs. Na/Na<sup>+</sup>), which corresponds to the pore filling of HC with the formation of Na clusters. The slope and plateau capacities of the pristine HC and Pre-HC anodes in full cells are summarized in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6e,f</a>. The slope capacities and plateau capacities are 165.1/85.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup> and 36.0/32.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup> for the full cell with the pristine HC during charge/discharge tests, a large decline of slope capacity and nearly equal plateau capacity mean that active Na<sup>+</sup> is mainly depleted in the slope region. Notably, slope capacities of full cells with Pre-HC during the charge test are reduced to 120.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup> for HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and 78.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup> for HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na, which are consistent with the results of half-cells (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting information). What's more, the ratio of plateau capacity increases in the full cell with Pre-HC anode in both charging and discharging tests owing to the reduced slope capacity after pre-sodiation, and the full cell with HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na shows larger plateau capacities (119.6/87.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup>) than that with HC-1&nbsp;µm Na (77.7/70.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>HC</sub><sup>−1</sup>) during charge/discharge tests, resulting in the increased amount of Na clusters in the pore of HC. Since the reversible capacity of the HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anode is larger than that of the NVP cathode (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting information), so extra Na could be stored in the HC matrix and make up for the active Na<sup>+</sup> loss during the cycle to improve the cycling stability of the full cell with Pre-HC. In general, smaller slope capacity and larger plateau capacity in the discharge and charge curve of Pre-HC indicate that the irreversible capacity of HC originating from Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption and intercalation in irreversible active sites is reduced after pre-sodiation. The lower working voltage range and larger reversible specific capacity of the Pre-HC anode can improve the energy density of the full battery.</p>
         
         <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
            <figure class="figure" id="adfm202403841-fig-0006"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e18af899-7349-46fd-902b-6310f249cc35/adfm202403841-fig-0006-m.jpg"><picture>
                     <source srcset="/cms/asset/e18af899-7349-46fd-902b-6310f249cc35/adfm202403841-fig-0006-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/303117cf-6abc-4791-b7ff-e97479e6094b/adfm202403841-fig-0006-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e18af899-7349-46fd-902b-6310f249cc35/adfm202403841-fig-0006-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                  <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 6<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adfm202403841-fig-0006&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadfm.202403841" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                  </div>
                  <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) The schematic picture of the Swagelok-type cell. Voltage profiles of Swagelok-type three-electrode cell with a Na metal reference electrode of b) NVP vs. the pristine HC, c) NVP vs. HC-1&nbsp;µm Na, and d) NVP vs. HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na, voltages of the full cell (dashed line), cathode (blue line) and anode (red line). The slope and plateau capacity during e) charge and f) discharge processes. The O 1s and F 1s XPS spectra of g,h) HC, i,j) HC-1&nbsp;µm Na and k,l) HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anodes, anodes were disassembled from full cells after 50 cycles.</div>
               </figcaption>
            </figure>
         </section>
         <p>It is generally accepted that the properties of SEI have great effects on the electrochemical performance of the battery,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0044" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0044_R_d212906234e1433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 44 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">44</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0045" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0045_R_d212906234e1433" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 45 - Energy Storage Mater.">45</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> thus depth-profiling XPS measurements were used to investigate the chemical composition evolution of SEI formed on the pristine and Pre-HC anodes after the 50<sup>th</sup> cycle, XPS data with etching for 0, 1 and 2&nbsp;min are shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6g–l</a>. It can be observed from O 1s spectra (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6g–i</a>) that C─O and C = O peaks dominate the outer surface of SEI, which originate from oxygenic organic components such as sodium alkyl carbonate (ROCO<sub>2</sub>Na) and sodium alkoxides (RONa),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0046" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0046_R_d212906234e1449" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 46 - J. Power Sources">46</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> with the increase of etching depth, inorganic components like Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>O, and C─O─Na emerge from the inner SEI layer, indicating that the organic-rich outer layer and inorganic-rich inner layer SEI are formed in the pristine and Pre-HC anodes. As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6j–l</a>, F 1s spectra could be deconvoluted into three components: NaF, P─F, and C─F peak. NaF is believed to arise from the reduction of FEC additive and the decomposition of NaPF<sub>6</sub>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0047" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0047_R_d212906234e1466" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 47 - Nano Energy">47</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> the P─F peak belongs to the decomposition products of NaPF<sub>6</sub> (such as Na<sub>x</sub>PF<sub>y</sub>, Na<sub>x</sub>PO<sub>y</sub>F<sub>z</sub>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0048_R_d212906234e1484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and the C─F peak arises from PVDF and residual FEC solvents. The relative intensities of NaF to C─F in the inner SEI layer of the Pre-HC anode as HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na or HC-1.0&nbsp;µm Na after etching are larger than that of the pristine HC.</p>
         
         <p>These differences in the relative content distribution of the SEI components should be related to the characteristics of the Pre-HC, which have been reported by many studies that pre-sodiation can promote the generation of SEI rich in inorganic components on the anodes.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0025_R_d212906234e1493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">25</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0031_R_d212906234e1493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - Adv. Energy Mater.">31</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0032_R_d212906234e1493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Angew. Chemie – Int. Ed.">32</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0049_R_d212906234e1493" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Infomat">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Ying Shirley Meng et&nbsp;al. attribute this to a substantial potential difference-driven SEI generation process that deviates from the thermodynamic stable state,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0050_R_d212906234e1498" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Adv. Energy Mater.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> significantly different from the close to the equilibrium state of SEI generation by slow C-rate charging and discharging. The augments of NaF and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> amount in the SEI of Pre-HC would hinder the transport of sodium ions (ion conductivity &lt;10<sup>−20</sup>&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0027_R_d212906234e1512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J. Power Sources">27</a>, <a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0051_R_d212906234e1512" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> as confirmed by the larger R<sub>SEI</sub> of full cells with the Pre-HC anodes in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5d,f</a>. After 50 cycles, as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6g–i</a>, the proportion of Na<sub>2</sub>O in the SEI of HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na is higher than that of HC and HC-1&nbsp;µm Na anodes, indicating the transformation of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> to Na<sub>2</sub>O in the unique SEI of Pre-HC-2.3&nbsp;µm Na anode, which was also discovered by Payam Kaghazchi et&nbsp;al.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0027_R_d212906234e1535" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - J. Power Sources">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Na<sub>2</sub>O can act as a sodium ion transport channel with higher conductivity (≈10<sup>−12</sup>&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>) than NaF and Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> (&lt;10<sup>−20</sup>&nbsp;S&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>), which is consistent with the anomalous variation of R<sub>SEI</sub> in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0005">5</a>. In brief, the SEI layer on the surface of Pre HC is rich in NaF, Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, and Na<sub>2</sub>O components, with Na<sup>+</sup> conduction but electronic insulation properties, which can alleviate electrolyte decomposition. In addition, the Pre-HC anode has a lower operating voltage range in the full cell cycle (as shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adfm202403841-fig-0006">6c,d</a>) if compared to the pristine HC, which may be conducive to the more uniform growth of SEI. Such inorganic-rich inner SEI of Pre-HC possesses better mechanical and chemical stability than that of pristine HC anode,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0037_R_d212906234e1572" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - Adv. Mater.">37</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which should play an important role in the improvement of the electrochemical performance of full batteries based on Pre-HC anodes. It is currently unclear why the internal SEI components are rich in NaF. In the future, more work is needed to explore the SEI evolution of Pre-HC anodes by the SSE reaction.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0030">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403841-sec-0030-title">3 Conclusion</h2>
         
         <p>In conclusion, a facile and precise electrode-level SSE pre-sodiation strategy is proposed to compensate for the irreversible capacity loss and improve the electrochemical performance of SIBs. This pre-sodiation method, without using any organic solution or liquid electrolyte, can avoid the introduction of inert species and by-products. What's more, a thin and unique inorganic-rich SEI layer was formed on the surface of the pre-sodiated HC by the spontaneous chemical reaction with electrolyte, which shall provide positive effects on the electrochemical performance of the Pre-HC anode. A comprehensive understanding of the effect of this pre-sodiation strategy was conducted by evaluating half-cells and full cells in two-electrode and three-electrode setups, a noticeable improvement in the ICE and over 90% pre-sodiation efficiency were obtained for the Pre-HC electrode. Thus, the ICEs of HC half-cells were enhanced from 76.0% to 107.9% after SSE pre-sodiation. As for the electrochemical performance of full cells, it was shown that Pre-HC vs. NVP full cell can obtain higher specific discharge capacity of 102.2&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> and ICE of 94.0% with better capacity retention of 69.1% than the full cell with pristine HC with only 66.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> specific discharge capacity, 61.0% ICE and 54.5% capacity retention. Moreover, the air stability of Pre-HC, as one critical but neglected issue in previous works, was discussed in this study. The pre-loaded sodium in pre-sodiated HC maintained the specific capacities of 671.1 and 418.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sub>Na</sub><sup>−1</sup> after being stored in a dry air atmosphere (dew-point temperature: −30&nbsp;°C, relative humidity: 1%) for 2 and 4&nbsp;h, respectively. We believe that the air stability of Pre-HC can be further improved in the practical battery assembly ambient, in which the dew-point temperature is usually below −45&nbsp;°C (relative humidity: 0.31%). Combined with the roll-to-roll device, this SSE pre-sodiation method, with the merits of process compatibility, high pre-sodiation capacity, and accuracy, is of great potential in practical application for both improved energy density and cycling stability of SIBs.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0040">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adfm202403841-sec-0040-title">4 Experimental Section</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0050">
            
            <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0060">
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0070">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403841-sec-0070-title"> Sample Preparation</h4>
                  
                  <p>The hard carbon (HC) electrodes were prepared by the slurry of 90&nbsp;wt% HC, 5&nbsp;wt% Super P, 5&nbsp;wt% PVDF and moderate NMP solvent, the slurry was cast onto a carbon-coated Al foil with a 120&nbsp;µm gap and then dried at 60&nbsp;°C for 12&nbsp;h. The mass loading of HC was 2.88&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. The Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP) electrodes were prepared with the same method with the active material mass loading of 5.26&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. The pre-sodiated HC (Pre-HC) electrodes were prepared by vacuum thermal evaporation, the evaporation rate was 1.5&nbsp;nm&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup>, sodium metal foils with the thicknesses of 1.0 and 2.3&nbsp;µm were deposited onto the as-prepared HC electrodes and then the Pre-HC electrodes were transferred into the Ar-filled glovebox (H<sub>2</sub>O &lt;1&nbsp;ppm, O<sub>2</sub> &lt;1&nbsp;ppm), the thickness of sodium foil was controlled by a quartz crystal microbalance. After sodium deposition, the electrodes were aged for 3–5 days under Ar atmosphere to ensure sufficient chemical reactions between sodium metal and HC.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0080">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403841-sec-0080-title"> Characterization</h4>
                  
                  <p>The chemical composition, structure, and morphology of HC and Pre-HC were investigated by X-ray diffractometer (XRD, Bruker D8 Advance), Raman spectroscopy (Renishaw InVia reflex), X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS, PHI-5000 VersaProbe III), Field-emission scanning electron microscope (FESEM, Hitachi Regulus 8100), transmission electron microscopy (TEM, JEOL ARM200F) and optical microscope (Gaopin, GP-660&nbsp;V). To avoid the chemical reactions of the Pre-HC with moisture, samples for XRD measurements were sealed by tape in an Ar-filled glove box, and XPS and SEM measurements were transferred by an Ar-filled sample holder. TEM characterizations were carried out with a cryo-transfer station.</p>
                  </section>
               
               <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adfm202403841-sec-0090">
                  
                  <h4 class="article-section__sub-title section4" id="adfm202403841-sec-0090-title"> Electrochemical Measurements</h4>
                  
                  <div class="paragraph-element">The half-cells and full cells were fabricated to CR-2032 coin-cells in an Ar-filled glove box (H<sub>2</sub>O&lt;1&nbsp;ppm, O<sub>2</sub>&lt;1&nbsp;ppm), 200&nbsp;µL 1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">M</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in a mixture of ethylene carbonate (EC) and ethyl methyl carbonate (EMC) in a 1:1, volume ratio&nbsp;with 2% fluoroethylene carbonate (FEC) was used as the electrolyte and glass microfiber filter as the separator. For the half-cell, the sodium disk was used as the reference electrode and counter electrode, while the full cell was assembled with HC or pre-sodiated HC as the anode and NVP as the cathode, and the capacity ratio of N/P was 1.15. Three-electrode cell (Swagelok-type) was fabricated with HC or Pre-HC anode, NVP cathode, and sodium disk as the reference electrode. The galvanostatic charge/discharge tests were performed on Neware battery testers (CT-4008) at room temperature. half-cells and full cells were cycled at 0.05&nbsp;C for the initial two cycles to form the stable interface, the voltage ranges were 0.01–2.0&nbsp;V for half-cells and 1.75–3.75&nbsp;V for full cells. The cyclic voltammetry (CV) test was performed on the CHI 660e workstation (Chenhua Co., Shanghai) at a scan rate of 0.1&nbsp;mV&nbsp;s<sup>−1</sup> between 0 and 2.0&nbsp;V. The electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) was measured by Zennium pro electrochemical workstation (Zahner, Germany) with an amplitude of 5&nbsp;mV in a frequency range from 100&nbsp;kHz to 50&nbsp;mHz. Galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) measurements were carried out with a constant charging/discharging current of 0.05&nbsp;C for 30&nbsp;min, followed by 30&nbsp;min of relaxation. The Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient can be calculated by the following equation simplified from Fick's second law:<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adfm202403841-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adfm202403841-bib-0052_R_d212906234e1660" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - J. Electrochem. Soc.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup><div class="inline-equation" id="adfm202403841-disp-0002"><span class="inline-equation__construct"><!--FIGURE-->

                  </section>
               </section>
            </section>
         </section>
